   6
01( ] W - Broken Wall (Either open or constantly shifting)
02(A] X - Wall (Cannot pass)
03(A] D - Door
04( ] P - Pillar (Def + 1, Avoid + 20)
05(X] C - Chest
06( ] (02,02) - Bullion (M)
07( ] (02,23) - Recover
08( ] (02,24) - Change Seal
09( ] B - Boss
10( ] E - Enemy
11( ] K - Chrom
12( ] N - Nah (Speak with Nowi / Nono or Chrom)
13( ]
14( ] This map can be difficult. There are a lot of ranged units, and all are
15( ] class 2 enemies. There are plenty of Dark Knights, Warriors, Sorecerors,
16(X] and Generals all over the map. Some of the Sorcerors wield tomes that
17( ] have a greater range than normal so can attack you at quite the
18( ] distance.
19( ]
20( ] Remember to bring someone who can open the chests, as well as Nowi, as
21(X] Chrom cannot recruit Nah on his own.
22( ]
23( ] The walls on this level break and fix themselves at different times on
24( ] different turns. There are doors that will remain open once you open
25( ] them, but do not rely on the walls to protect you from enemies in the
other halls, as they may break down the next turn.

Keep your units doubled and in defensive positions at all times, be ready for
enemies to come through broken walls at the worst possible moment. The walls
are triggered by the area you're in, so the wall to Nah will break down when
you come close to it (in that hallway). However, with this other walls will
start to break to allow the enemy to attack you.

You should be fine so long as you are able to open the doors and hence not
rely on the walls, but it is best to keep away from them just to be sure.

Note that hugging the wall can still put you under fire from ranged enemies,
so keep ranges in mind!

Also, beware of Warriors with the Counter skill, this can be frustrating if
you rely on close quarters units especially.

    Turn 4: Wyvern Lord
    Turn 5: Dark Flier / Wyvern Lord (Lunatic Only)
7 - Turn 5: Wyvern Lord (Lunatic Only)
8 - Turn 5: Falcon Knight (Lunatic Only)
K - Chrom
A - Allied Deploy Space

As you can see from the above, this map is heavily reinforcement based. It
is a defensive level, a ring of woods around Tiki for you to station your
units. The enemies come in waves of reinforcements. They are all flying
units, so bows and wind magic will be super effective. You must protect Tiki
if you want to get her after the level.

There are multiple ways you can go about this map. Either take the defensive
and line your units up in the trees, making sure to bring archers and other
wind mages as you deal with only flying units on this level, and put stronger
defensive units in front to take the brunt of the attack as you get them from
behind. Healers with physic will be useful too.

Another way is the more offensive strategy, where you can send groups of
units to the three points (west, south, and east) and just destroy the enemies
as they come into the map. This is very effective if you have the powerful
units to do so, and it ensures that none of the enemies even have a chance
to get close to Tiki. This guide gives you who and what comes from where on
which turn, so this should assist you on lining your units up (see map above).

You may end up somewhere between the woods and their spawn point, which is
optimal as it takes them until their third turn to attack Tiki, their first
will make them end up around this zone.

Note, however, that the enemies will priortize Tiki, and so usually fly by
the units that are standing to meet them. If you have Galeforce units, then
they will be useful in taking them down before they reach Tiki, but if not,
then I suggest a third strategy.

A third is a mix of the above two, some units stay with Tiki (can form a ring
around her to ensure that the flying units can't attack), while another
detachment goes off to fight them at their spawn points. This way even if one
slips by, the crew left with Tiki should be able to handle the remainder. You
may not want to double some units in order to attack multiple enemies as you
start to get swarmed in later turns. Dancers and Galeforce will come in handy
here.

Tiki will only be able to take one or two hits from her enemies, so be very
careful. The boss starts moving after all reinforcements are dead.

01(E] H = Mountains / Peak
02(H] T = Woods (Def + 1, Avo + 10)
03(H] F = Fort (Def + 2, Avo + 10, Heal + 20)
04(H] X = Building
05(H] V = Village (Rescue)
06(H] B = Boss
07(H] E = Enemy
08(H] K = Chrom
09(H] A = Allied Deploy Space
10(H] M = Emmeryn (Ensure she survives in order to recruit her; talk with
11( ]     Chrom)
12( ]
13( ] This map can be straightforward or hard depending how you have been
14( ] playing up until now. If you have been grinding and have super-powerful
15( ] characters, then this map will be simple as any other. If not, then I
16(T] suggest bringing units with high mobility and self sufficiency.
17( ]
18(M] The enemy goes after Emmeryn pretty quickly, she will be killed by the
19( ] second turn by the Assassin running toward her. As such, you have to
20( ] rush a group over to save her. If you have a flying unit paired up with
21(H] a unit who has Galeforce, it is really easy to get there. Add a dancer
22(H] to the mix and you will have insane mobility and have no problem dealing
23(H] with the enemies heading toward her. She does not move at all, and will
24(H] not be in use even after you talk to her. So keep an eye on her that no
25(H] flying units get around you and attack her. Viewing enemy ranges may
26(H] help in this regard.

The enemy has a general strategy, they attack you with the few sages lined up
along the middle-mountain area with long ranged attacks, and said their
Griffon Riders to ambush your units as you head east to Emmeryn. The group
in the west will come down and around the left side of the mountain where the
village is. The village offers a rescue staff, so you do not need to send a
significant detachment that way, maybe one or two units that can fetch it and
then regroup with the east group. Or, if they are strong enough, can get the
item, then sit in the woods at (11,22) and handle the west enemies so they
won't be a threat to Emmeryn.

When you save Emmeryn and handle the advancing enemy units, then you can
move up around the east, taking advantage of the few forts around where the
boss is. He's not too hard to deal with, but do not get careless! Be wary of
the Dark Knights all around him.

X = Wall/Impassable Terrain
C = Cliff
S = Spring
W = Stairway
N = Coffin
K = Chrom
A = Allied Deployment Space
B = Boss
E = Enemy
Y = Yen'fay (NPC; speak with Say'ri only)

Bring Say'ri (assuming she's still alive). She is the only one who can
recruit Yen'fay.

A fairly enclosed map with quite a few high speed and skill enemies
(Swordmasters, Assassins, and hard hitting Heroes, as well as Tricksters).
There are no magic enemies on this map, so high defense and speed units are
recommended. A General can usually plow through pretty easily, especially
with a high defense counter and paired up with a speedy unit.

To recruit Yen'fay, speak to him with Say'ri, you will want to get to him
fairly quickly so he doesn't rush off on his own to get killed. He will come
to you if you have enemies nearby. He becomes playable right after the
conversation.

As long as your units are grouped, and have a good balance of speed and
defense, they will clear this map very easily. It becomes a steady march
north to defeat the boss after Yen'fay is secure.

24[X][X][ ][ ][ ][ ][X][A][A][A][A][X][ ][ ][V][ ][X][X]
25[X][X][ ][ ][ ][ ][X][ ][ ][ ][ ][X][ ][ ][ ][ ][X][X]

X - Wall
W - Spring
B - Boss
A - Allied Deploy Spaces
K - Chrom
V - Aversa (Recruited if she confronts herself and survives the chapter)
E - Enemy (Will be whoever you bring on the level! If you bring less than the
           max amount [as in leave any space empty], some of your units will
           be duplicated instead)

So this chapter can be very difficult or very easy. It depends what units you
bring on it. If you bring your usual party of destroyers -- you will be
facing your own party of destroyers -- and that can be difficult!

So you can bring a bunch of weaklings instead, if you have any. If not, you
can go get some easy Spotpass people (such as Florina) and then hope they
get duplicated, and bring one or two strong people to easily sweep the floor
with them all.

Though, it may backfire and you are left with a bunch of weak ones versus your
few strong units that were cloned. Be careful!

The enemy will be aggressive, and Boss Aversa will go after ally Aversa.
Ensure Aversa survives if you want her! Let her attack herself, she should
be able to survive one attack. Have someone nearby to take the boss out
swiftly afterward. This chapter should not take long at all!

==============================================================================

DLC CHAPTERS                                                            [DLCC]

==============================================================================

This section is for a overview of the DLC, avaliable in the in-game store.
These can be played via the Otherworld Gate on the map (Activated after
Chapter 06 in the story0. As long as the DLC is on the console, it is not
limited to any particular playthrough.

These Chapters can be replayed as many times as you like, allowing one to
grind for experience, items, etc. If you already have the character that is
recruitable, the game will give you a choice to retain your character and
their current stats, or reset them (starting anew).

The DLC usually offers either a character, or special items, or both. There
are many cameos from previous games; such as maps, characters, and music.
Conversations can be had between characters you bring with other particular
characters from previous titles.

This section is mainly under construction, as I want to prioritize the main
walkthrough first! Though if more people want the DLC to be prioritized to
know what to expect, I will focus on it.

DLC Chapters:

Below is a quick highlight of DLC and their prices. The DLC title, dates,
and unlocked characters/items are listed.

The title in quotations is the English name. The one below it is the Japanese
one. The dates in the first paranthesis are the Japanese dates, the one on
the right is for the US, with price in USD.

Since they're releasing in a different order, some in map packs for the US,
I decided to bunch them by series rather than order of release.

Below is the series information with split sections!

==============================================================================
CHARACTER GUIDE/RECRUITMENT                                             [CHAR]
==============================================================================

How to get all the characters, including child characters, their base stats,
opinions, etc!

Warning! Spoilers may be abound! Please proceed with caution!

This is the basic format!

[XXXX]
Name:
Class:
When/How:
Other Classes:
Support:
Generation:
Children/Parent:
Possible Children: (Male only)
Base Stats:
X [HP]  XX 
X [STR] XX 
X [MAG] XX
X [SKL] XX
X [SPD] XX
X [LUC] XX
X [DEF] XX
X [RES] XX
Weapon Level (S): X
Birthday:
Death Quote:
Character Bio:
Opinion:

Explanation for Basic Format!

[XXXX] The search box!

Name: Their Name

Class: Initial Class: The class they are when you get them.

When/How: How to recruit!

Other Classes: What they can become (includes both Upgrade and Class 
               Swapping)

Support: Who they can support (Anyone with * is marriable, A/S means max
         support level.)
 -Note: My Unit can support everyone so will not appear on every list to 
        avoid redundancy.
 -Note: Generation I units will be able to support whoever their children are
        up to A level, and they will not appear on the lists (instead they
        will be in "Possible children/children" lists. This is also to avoid
        clutter. In the Child's profile, possible parents will also appear
        in the same way. The same applies to siblings / non siblings.

Generation: (Generation I means Initial "parents", Generation II means child)

Children: (Who the child will be if Generation I if mother, and who the
           possible children can be if father. Exceptions exist.)
 -Note: Morgan will be anyone's son/daughter depending on 
        My Unit's gender, and will not be listed under all characters 
        aside from My Unit.
Parent: (Who the parent (mother) will be if Generation II)

Possible Children/Parent: This will be what children one can have depending
                          on relationships, and what possible parents the
                          children can have.

             below. For information on each stat, check Vital Translatons).
 -Note: X represents growth rates, from E (bad) to A (good). These come from
        the official guide, and will be posted until proved to be mistaken
        otherwise.

Note on Stats: Max stats can vary by character and class. It would be too
complicated to write out here, so I will redirect you to a very useful
set up on serenesforest.net to view maximum stats:

http://www.serenesforest.net/fe13/char_max_all.html

at least. Children stats vary due to inheritance.

(As appears on the field, if applicable)
(As appears in the Barracks)

Character Title: The Epilogue title for the character (Possibly)

Opinion: My Opinion of them (How they were as a unit, personality, etc). This
         obviously does not mean "Use or don't use" said units, as it is just
         experience in one playthrough, and the more dedicated could probably
         provide better explanations/suggestions.

         Though in the end I like to say it comes down to your own preference,
         especially in this game where one can reclass units constantly and
         max their stats out, I suppose some skills are still limited to
         certain characters, though.

         Remember: Opinion is exactly that. Like a game review, or like what
         any random person says -- do not take these as the absolute final
         word.

Generation I

 -Note: Includes Story-Specific Generation II Character
 -Note: Use Ctrl + F to skip to their section! Be sure to include the brackets
        so you don't keep running into every single mention of them.
 -Note: Mothers always have the same children, fathers effect their hair color,
        classes they can become (if applicable), and stats growth (?)
 -Note: Skills are passed down to children from parents
 -Note: Exceptions to the above are noted in their respective sections.
 -Note: Sidequests for the children unlock the moment an S rank is reached
        between parents, and it is after Chapter 14

[MYUN]

Name: Avatar / MyUnit
Class: Lv 1 Strategist -> Grandmaster
When/How: Automatic; Prologue
Other Classes: All (Male/Female slightly Varies, check Class section)
Support: 
 -Everyone (Can Marry Anyone of Opposite Gender; including Anna, Tiki, etc)
Generation: I
Children: Morgan (Opposite Gender to My Unit, with whoever
                is partner. Will be related to offspring and not be able to
                marry them even if they could otherwise. Can also marry into
                Generation II!)
Possible Children (Male): All other marriable units' children; Morgan (Female)
                  (Female): Morgan (Male), Lucina
Base Stats:
[HP]  19
[STR] 06 
[MAG] 05 
[SKL] 05 
[SPD] 06 
[LUC] 04 
[DEF] 06 
[RES] 04
Weapon Level (S): Sword (E) Magic (E)
-Note: Growth rates not listed until I am sure how it works with attributing
 good and bad traits. If you have information on this, please contact me.
Skills:
-Veteran
Birthday: Whatever you set it as.
Epilogue Title: "High Deliverer"
Death Quote:
Character Bio:
"A traveler with no memory of the past, but a gift for tactics."
"A traveler who remembers nothing prior to being found by the wayside. Chrom
realized her/his tactical genius and enlisted her/him in the Shepherds, where
she/he is well liked. THe biggest mystery of the group."

Opinion: The character is pretty interesting in the sense that they can
support *everyone*. That is certainly unique and gives a good insight on
the character, though may also detach the player as there's no decision
making or anything involved.

In terms of classes and such, MyUnit gets to be every class of their gender
(with some exceptions), certainly making them a very malleable and
formiddable unit, likely to be one of your most superior units in the game.
Check classes and their skills, as well as growth rates to determine which
skills you want in the end to fit your character best. There is no end to
customization here.

Considering they can support *everyone*, there is obviously a lot of dialogue
that can either make you feel closer (or farther) from MyUnit. But there are
quite a few degrees of freedom in there as a result too, though it may remind
one of a dating sim, be it for good or bad.

[CHRO]

Name: Chrom / Krom
Class: Lv 1  Lord -> Great Lord
When/How: Automatic; Prologue
Other Classes:
 -Cavalier -> Paladin / Great Knight
 -Archer -> Sniper / Bow Knight
Support:
 -Lissa     A
 -Frederick A
 -Vaike     A
 -Gaius     A
*-Sumia     S
*-Sully     S
*-Maribelle S
*-Olivia    S
Generation: I
Possible Children: 
-Lucina, Cynthia, Kjelle, Brady, Inigo
Base Stats:
C [HP]  20
C [STR] 07 
E [MAG] 01
C [SKL] 08
C [SPD] 08 
A [LUC] 05
D [DEF] 07
E [RES] 01
Weapon Level (S): Sword (E)
Skills:
-Dual Attack+
Birthday: 5/27
Death Quote:
Epilogue Title: "Newly Exalted"
Character Bio:
"Captain of the Shepherds. Treats his men firmly but fairly."
"The prince of Ylissle and descendant of the Hero-King. While of noble blood,
he also leads a militia known as the Shepherds. His strong conviction makes
him a fine captain. The most likely to break things."

Opinion: Chrom, being one of the main characters of the game, you have to
use whether you like it or not for all non-skirmish and side missions. For
that reason, you will have to get used to him whether you like him or not!

Fortunately, he manages to hold his own on the lower difficulties right from
the start, and has the advantage of being able to use a weapon that does not
break. He has a pretty limited class set, but is able to become a Great Lord,
a very nice and well rounded class that learns Aether.

With this, if made into a Paladin, he can learn Aegis, which can go in good
combination with it.

His supports are pretty limiting too, you would expect more from the Lord of
the game, and so he doesn't actually get much room for background development
via his supports.

"A Shepherd, and Chrom's little sister. Eager to prove herself."
"Chrom's tomboyish little sister, the princess of Ylissle. With nary an ounce
of nobility in her personality, she is among the most likeable and approachable
of the Shepherds. The girl most likely to snort."

Opinion: She starts off rather fragile, and continues to be as you advance
her. She has nice class options, notably Pegasus Knight and hence Dark Flier,
meaning she is capable of passing on Galeforce to her son, Owain.

Though she can be a Battle Cleric, her strength often falls short for the
point of using an axe, though the skill to get as a Battle Cleric (Renewal)
is very useful with Galeforce, and with Miracle as well. She works nicely as
a Valkyrie or Sage as an ending class, as they are magic based.

Her personality is rather up beat, though "tomboy" is not exactly the word
I would use to describe her.

Lunatic mode where his services are especially needed. In later game, you
may find more use for him when reclassing to a lower class in order to get
him more skills and experience.

Personality wise, he's just about the most loyal person you'll find around,
as evident in his lovely support conversations, such as with Chrom.

through, or maybe I am just terribly unlucky!

He has a variety in classes to choose from, from the more magical path to the
flying path. This means he does get a variety of skills, but you may end up
with characters that you prefer to use while Virion gets benched.

It's a shame, though, since his personality via supports is very amusing.

improve after some grinding as she has a fair choice of classes (both a
Paladin and Swordmaster, etc), meaning she has a nice range of skills that
she can learn and pass on to her child.

Her growths in Skill and Speed are better than her counterpart, Stahl. But
her Strength and Defense fall shorter.

down to whoever you decide for his children to be.

making her a fully magic-based unit.

Weapon Level (S): Lance (D)

Character Bio:
"A clumsy asipring Shepherd who tries her best all the same."
"An absentminded, klutzy Shepherd with a shocking lack of self-worth. However,
she exhibits one-of-a-kind talent, particulary when it comes to working with
animals. The best at tripping over nothing."

Opinion: Sumia, the clumsy. She is a fairly well rounded unit in categories
other than magic. Her range of classes vary too, everything from the Dark
Flier to a General, neither of them really fitting to her character, but
a big boost in the skills she can learn and pass down to her daughter.

She has a surprisingly limited range of supports, and the game goes to great
lengths to say, "We're totally not trying to pair her up with Chrom" (even
titling her rescue cutscene as "lovebirds")

Her personality may get a little obnoxious.

She is one of two Pegasus Knights in the game, the other being Cordelia, who
worked out much better. However, they both have differing range of classes,
meaning a differing range of skill sets, and so it can come down to personal
preference.

well as a Battle Priest. This makes him open to an insane amount of useful
skills that when on a General or Great Knight, would just be deadly. A
General with Acrobat, Lethality, and Renewal for instance.

Character wise, he lacks presence, and this joke carries over quite a bit in
his support conversations. He should have been the only character with the
"Shade" or "Stillness" skill (which do not exist in this game).

Character Bio:
"A villager from a remote corner of Ylisse who came to the fight with little

Opinion: A big complaint about Donnel is that the Villager class cannot
upgrade into anything directly. The useful thing about his base class is
learning the "Underdog" skill at Level 15. After that, he must be
changed to a different class before upgrading to a newer one.

He works out okay thanks to the extra level up opportunities he gets, but
when you train your other units diligently, it comes down to preference. If
you have time to train him, however, he becomes an incredible unit, especially
when made a Hero (personal favorite). He will likely max out most of his stats
thanks to his great growths compounded with his skills, so it comes down to
whichever class you prefer.

He has a great skill and class range, a lot of hard hitting classes with
useful skills.

You may want to consider who he passes this skill down to. He is the only
one with it in the game.

B [HP]  28

"The last of the taguel race. Sensible and self-reliant."
"A nationless shape-shifter and the last of the taguel. While cool and
sensible by nature, she shows little interest in finding a partner and
remedying the fate of her race. The fastest at wolfing down a meal."

Opinion: Reminiscent of Manakete of this game and Laguz of previous games,
Panne is a manner of preference. Her growth is all over the place, getting
good growths in the physical sectors of strength, speed, defense, etc. When
you first get her in the game, access to stones are limited and so you may
have trouble training her beyond the first stone use. Her base stats without
the stone may be rather low, and so you may be best changing her to another
class first.

Her class range is fairly open, being a Thief leaves her to eventually
become an Assassin class, which may be useful. Leaving her as a Taguel is
often rare due to the limitations in weaponry, so I would advise not doing
so.

Her personality is as expected of a genocide-sole-survivor. She's not above
rabbit jokes, however. If MyUnit is paired with her, Morgan will be able
to shift into a Taguel as well.

uncomfortable with her child-like demeanor (in looks and personality). While

suppose it comes down to preference in this sense.

Character Bio:
"An enigmatic merchant with a bevy of identical sisters --more than she can

Opinion: Anna is a very useful unit when you first get her, and she ends with

Another downside is her support is very limited to MyUnit and Tiki, meaning
she won't receieve the same benefits as other units with plenty of supports
may. For these reasons she may fall behind in the later game.

Her other classes can be useful, but Trickster/Assassin may be the best for
her.

Weapon Level (S): Sword (D)

Death Quote:
Character Bio:
"A shy, introverted caravan dancer who goes above and beyond to help others.

Opinion: She's the only dancer you get in this game! She's a very useful unit,

she's easy to level up since the dancing gives experience! She will do really
nicely in the luck and speed category, so will often be able to dodge in those
vital moments.

Eventually I made her an Assassin, and a Swordmaster, then back to Dancer.
That way, she was able to not only dance, but also defend herself by using
the skills Astra or Lethality, etc.

The overly shy personality may get annoying for some, but to those it was
aiming to appeal to here (in Japan), it certainly worked! She is still a good
unit for support regardless of that.

She is the hardest to pair with Chrom, as you have to make sure every other
compatible female unit is married off.

Can be a Parent to Morgan (If My Unit is Male)
Parent: Chrom
Possible Mothers: S Supports with Chrom
Base Stats:
C [HP]  12
D [STR] 05
E [MAG] 01
C [SKL] 08
C [SPD] 04
A [LUC] 13
D [DEF] 03
D [RES] 03
Weapon Level (S): Sword (C)
Birthday: 4/20
Death Quote:
Character Bio:
"Chrom's future daugher, a kind and just princess who made it her duty to
save the world. She loves her fatehr and would do anything to keep him safe.
The least likely to get a joke."

Opinion: She was probably my overall most successful unit, with the best 
performence overall. MyUnit had married Chrom, and so she had inherited
every avaliable Female class, and so could acquire any skill of those classes
if changed and trained to the required levels.

Considering she had already started with Aether among other things, as well
as the ability to support my other most often used units (i.e. MyUnit, Krom,
Wood, Mark (who was a sibling), etc, and then paired with the fact she also
gets an infinite weapon all came down to her being an incredible unit during
my playthrough. I settled on Great Lord in the end as I liked the model
best, and the well rounded stats, over the other classes she could be.

I also like her design, a bit less on the fanservice side. She was voted
quite the popular character in Japan in polls from The Knights of Iris. I'm
not sure how she compares in the west, so far I have seen more favor on other
characters.

In terms of personality, she's quite the loyal one, with a strong exterior and
a softer interior. Some with a degree of understanding of Japanese (and even
those without) may get tired of her saying Otou-sama (My Lord-father),
a lot, or Okaa-sama (My Lord-Mother) a lot, but I forgave her for it
when you understand the circumstance of where she's coming from (that is, a
world where everyone's parents are dead).

Being her parent makes a few events in the story also seem more relevant,
such as the confrontation scene.

Trivia: Her birthday is the same as the release of the first Fire Emblem
game.

Birthday: 2/28
Death Quote: "I won't have to be alone...anymore..."
Character Bio:
"The Voice of the divine dragon. While mature, she also has a child-like
side. Being a dragonkin, she has lived since days of yore and was friends
with the Hero-King, Marth. The most likely to sleep in."

Opinion: A cameo from the older games, just a little more grown up. She comes
a little latish in the game, but if you like to grind in skirmishes to bring
people up to speed, she will probably work nicely! But at this point I imagine
you would already have a select group of powerful units that may end up
benching Tiki anyway. It all just comes down to how you play! She starts off
with the Dragonstone+ though, which boosts her stats incredibly while she
uses it.

Her HP and Luck will go up almost guaranteed, the rest of her stats often
follow for overall good level ups.

Though her story presence is off and on, she's still able to die and remain
dead for the epilogue.

I reclassed her into a Wyvern Rider when she maxed out her Manakete level,
and she did okay there too, but not as good as my already existing flying
units. So it comes down to your preference and patience, really! When she
upgraded into a Wyvern Lord from there, she did extremely well; again, it
depends how much you grind/would use her in late game.

Due to design, she's really popular here (in Japan) as you can imagine! She
has quite a bit of fan art of her as well that you can easily find on places
like pixiv! Personality wise, despite the exterior can still be a little
childish. The supports with the female MyUnit is pretty silly.

Death Quote:
Character Bio:
"The West-Khan of Regna Ferox. His rival, Flavia, calls him "oaf" due to his
attitude, but he is actually quite quick witted. He exhibits a fatherly side
around Chrom's group. The guy with the biggest reactions."

Opinion: His story presence is great, but by the time you get him as a
playable character, the average party and equivalent level of Warrior may
be doing much better than him. He has good HP and attack going for him,
but his speed and defense start to lag behind what others you may have.

You get him on the third last chapter of the game, so storywise he may not
be too useful, but if messing around with skirmishes and such before the
last level, you may find some use!

Personally, I think his funky clothing is awesome, and seems to have set the
standard for the warrior model, which may look awkward on other characters
(like Donnel or Henry...) He also has a lovely laugh.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Generation II

-Note: Section still in progress.
-Note: MyUnit can still form relationships with everyone in this generation,
       but relationships will only produce Morgan.
-Note: All Generation II units will have A supports with their mother, and
       A supports with whoever their father is. As such, all possible
       fathers are not listed at the moment.
-Note: Alternate classes (the ones that they don't start off as) are inherited
       from the parent's alternate classes. MyUnit's children will have all
       classes avaliable to that gender unlocked. For now, the sections do
       not contain all possible classes from all fathers. Check father's
       class options to determine what the child will have in addition of
       what they inherit from their mother (already shown).
-Note: Skills are passed down from parents
-Note: Base stats and growths and such vary greatly pending on parents!
-Note: Sidequests unlock the moment an S rank is reached with the parents,
       and if the story is after Chapter 13.
-Note: Children can usually be recruited by their Mothers or Krom, but
       exceptions are noted, such as Nah.
-Note: Morgan, Lucina have varying supports; For Example: If you are Lucina's
       parent, there will be a separate branch of supports than if you were
       not. Mark likewise, if related to a character, will have a different
       branch of supports. If Chrom marries another female aside from MyUnit,
       that child will be related to Lucina, etc.
-Note: Generation II can marry (with no children with the exception of
       (MyUnit/Avatar), but cannot marry with those who may be siblings (such
       as if Chrom marries Olivia, then Inigo cannot be with Lucina).

[LUCI]

Name: Lucina
Class: Lv 10 Lord -> Great Lord
When/How: Automatic; Chapter 13 End
Other Classes:

       Will inherit Mother's Class-possibilities in addition to below.
-Note: This Profile is in both Gen I and II's lists
 -Cavalier -> Paladin / Great Knight
 -Archer -> Sniper / Bow Knight

*-Gerome  S
*-Morgan  S (If Male and not Brother)
Generation: I/II (Marriable with Kids, Yet...)
Children: 
Can be a Parent to Morgan (If My Unit is Male)
Parent: Chrom
Possible Mothers: S Supports with Chrom
Base Stats:
C [HP]  12
D [STR] 05
E [MAG] 01
C [SKL] 08
C [SPD] 04
A [LUC] 13
D [DEF] 03
D [RES] 03
Weapon Level (S): Sword (C)
Birthday: 4/20
Death Quote:
Character Bio:
"Chrom's future daugher, a kind and just princess who made it her duty to
save the world. She loves her fatehr and would do anything to keep him safe.
The least likely to get a joke."

Opinion: She was probably my overall most successful unit, with the best 
performence overall. MyUnit had married Chrom, and so she had inherited
every avaliable Female class, and so could acquire any skill of those classes
if changed and trained to the required levels.

Considering she had already started with Aether among other things, as well
as the ability to support my other most often used units (i.e. MyUnit, Krom,
Wood, Mark (who was a sibling), etc, and then paired with the fact she also
gets an infinite weapon all came down to her being an incredible unit during
my playthrough. I settled on Great Lord in the end as I liked the model
best, and the well rounded stats, over the other classes she could be.

I also like her design, a bit less on the fanservice side. She was voted
quite the popular character in Japan in polls from The Knights of Iris. I'm
not sure how she compares in the west, so far I have seen more favor on other
characters.

In terms of personality, she's quite the loyal one, with a strong exterior and
a softer interior. Some with a degree of understanding of Japanese (and even
those without) may get tired of her saying Otou-sama (My Lord-father),
a lot, or Okaa-sama (My Lord-Mother) a lot, but I forgave her for it
when you understand the circumstance of where she's coming from (that is, a
world where everyone's parents are dead).

Being her parent makes a few events in the story also seem more relevant,
such as the confrontation scene.

Trivia: Her birthday is the same as the release of the first Fire Emblem
game, and FE9: Path of Radiance.

Character Bio:
"Cordelia's future daughter. Growing up in the shadow of her mother has given

get her way. The most wasteful shopper."

the high skill stat, and when you have Lethality with Galeforce (which she 
can either inherit or learn on her own), she becomes incredibly useful.

Pending on the father, you can compound onto that skill set to make quite the
able Hero or whatever class you choose.

Personality wise she may not be the nicest to talk to, but I believe the
"tsundere"-ish character is appealing to many the game is geared toward. She
shares a love-hate relationship with most with deep seated mommy-issues as
the game itself describes. 

Her relationship with characters if often the same sort of relationship fans
of older Fire Emblem games (and myself) share with this game...

Trivia: Her birthday is the same as the release of FE3: Mystery of the

generally tends to shoot way up, making her quite the speedy unit. While
her default class set has the useful Sorceror, pending on the father, she
can perform really well.

Her personality has interesting...twists.

Opinion: The level she is recruited on is one of the harder ones. She is
one of the few who can support Tiki as well.

She can be a useful Manakete, and will often perform better than her mother
when trained to do so, but if not training her, then you may have better
units by this point in the game anyway.

Her father is important as it will open new class options to her, so one may
want to think on who to pair Nowi with in order to better Nah.

Trivia: Her birthday is the same as the release of FE6: Sword of Seals.

Character Bio:
"The wild and ruthless former king of Plegia. He once took sick pleasure in
hurting others, but his own life was not easy, and he has shown signs of

Opinion: Very interesting that he's just up and about without anyone caring,
but for the sake of gameplay, here he is. Also nothing in the supports about
his plot and...never mind.

He's a pretty good unit, and has quite the range of useful classes he can
become, and hence useful skills. He can only support MyUnit, and Morgan can
have a very interesting father as a result...

However, like with other Bonus Box characters, you get him in the "post game,"
pretty much, making him not too useful for actual story missions.

Opinion: The Conqueror is back. Somehow, since Chrom has this bad habit of not
putting down his opponents.

He is an amazing unit, as you can see, with his unique class and skill that
comes with it. He will be good no matter what class you put him in, with
his max weapon skills and very useful Conqueror skill.

You get him right after the last level, though, making him pretty much a
"post game" unit, so may not have any actual uses for the main campaign.

"Chrom's elder sister, the former exalt of Ylisse. A fall in Plegia took most

Opinion: It seems nobody remains dead in this game... it sort of trivializes 
the whole point of... well you get the point!

Her class selection is fairly limited, and covers a range of skills that may
be useful if ending as a Sage, but nothing substantial. You get her incredibly
late due to being a Bonus Box paralogue, and hence right at the end of the
game. Her start stats are probably lower than any other magic user you would
have by this point.

She's only able to support MyUnit, not even Chrom or Lissa, a little odd on
the developers' part.

The game makes fun of itself with how people don't stay dead on the chapter
you get Yen'fay.

Like the other units you get via Bonus Box, you probably already have other
units of his class that have far surpassed him in everyway. He has fair
luck and HP growth, and looks pretty cool aesthetically, but that's all
he has going for him...

other late comers via sidequests and bonus boxes, a good unit, but you probably
have better units by now.

With limited supports, she loses out on bonuses that others may have on the
field.

Personality wise, well everything in the story was a lie, and she gives you
a quick tragic backstory that doesn't really convince anyone. I'm sure some
are fond of the seductive sort of person, though. Her design looks all over
the place.

Stats: Min.   Max. Growth Rates
  [HP]  XX     XX       X
  [STR] XX     XX       X          
  [MAG] XX     XX       X

  [SPD] XX     XX       X

Who can: (Who can become this class)
 -Note: Regarding children, as inheriting the class option is dependent on
        the parents, only those that have a class by default will be noted.
        For information on what they can become with a certain father, just
        see the potential classes their fathers can become).
 -Note: All the SpotPass characters can generally become any class with a
        few exceptions. They are not noted under what they can become, only
        under what they start as, and maybe not even that).
 -Note: MyUnit can become any class in their gender set (see above), and so
        will not be listed as "Can" in every section).
 -Note: Morgan can also be any class due to being MyUnit's son/daughter.
        Morgan can be a special class IF the daughter of characters of a
        special class. (Daughter due to male being able to pick a mate).

Class Opinion: TBA

[MSLD]

Class Name: Great Lord
Class Type: II
Promotes from: Lord
Movement: 6 ; Type: Normal
Double Effects: Speed + 4, Luck + 4
Natural Skills: 
-Lv 05: Aether
-Lv 15: Rightful King
Stats:  Min.   Max. Growth Rates
  [HP]  23/20  80/80       C
  [STR] 10/08  43/40       C          
  [MAG] 00/01  30/30       E          
  [SKL] 07/09  40/42       C         
  [SPD] 09/11  40/44       C          
  [LUC] 00/00  45/45       E          
  [DEF] 10/08  42/40       D          
  [RES] 03/04  40/40       D          
(Note: Left side of the "/": Male, Right side of the "/": Female)
Weapons: Sword, Lance
Who: None
Who can:
-Chrom
-Lucina

Class Opinion: A great class to default upgrade to, especially with the well
rounded stats and exclusivity to just two characters! The skill Aether is
also really useful, both restoring HP and likely KOing the enemy. The fact
that Lucina and Krom also get an infinite weapon (A sword that doesn't
break) really helps this class out too for the both of them. I recommend
after you have given them whichever skills you want, you put them back to
this class.

There is no story limitation as there usually is with Lords in other games,
either! So you can upgrade Krom at any point if he is above Level 10 and
you have the right item.

If Lucina is MyUnit's child, then you can allocate even more of other class's
skills to this one!

MyUnit, however, any others you meet via SpotPass or StreetPass also can be
any class and this as a default.

The Veteran skill is very useful too, in terms of giving you a lot
of experience!

Class Type: II

-Lv 15: Swordfaire

a Myrmidon! Later on though, the maximum stats start to fall short when up
against heaviny protected enemies, you'll attack quickly but likely do no
damage due to the low strength, unfortunately...

Otherwise, the skill Astra is very useful to have, as well as the boost
in Skill and Speed growth for those who need it!

Class Opinion: A quick and hard hitting unit! The Assassin class sacrifices

In just looks alone, I think they look pretty cool! Both male and female.

Class Opinion: Warriors are a pretty useful class. It's a shame they are a
male only class though, a Female Warrior would have been interesting!

Anyway, at maximum strength this class is quite the powerhouse, the fact
they can also use Bows adds to this, making them a deadly ranged and melee
unit. Resistance and magic remain low, so just keep away from too many
magical encounters, though they will likely kill the magician if they attack
first. Maybe mixing it up with Vantage if possible would be useful when in
danger!

Also, the skill Counter makes for a very nice defensive enemy HP reducing
move! So for those who can become warriors, it may be a useful skill to get
and pass down to children too.

==============================================================================
SKILLS                                                                  [SKIL]
==============================================================================

All the skills in the game, the classes that unlock them, what they do, etc
will be posted here!

Note: While some of the translations are a little questionable (not to any
      large extent!) I'll keep with the SN names for the skills section for
      now! This section is still being updated to include the Japanese
      Characters, that way you can look them up by characters to see which
      logo is which skill!

I am currently changing skills to their English names and descriptions as
they come.

Format:

Skill Name
Skill Effect/What it does/etc
Skill Type: Auto/Command/Stat Based Activation
 -Auto       = Always in effect
 -Command    = Has to use the "Aid" function on the map, outside of battle
 -Stat Based = Pending on unit stats
Class (That learns it) 
Lv (XX) (Level it is learned at)
Logo Description: Just a quick picture description (Not yet completed)
Who: (Who starts off with it, this section may not be completed)

for Fame Points!

Item Name (X/X) [Uses], XXXX G (Cost)
 -Note: If cost is "----", cannot be bought in stores

Vulnerary (3/3) 300 G 
 -Restores 10 HP to user on use

Concoction (3/3) 600 G
 -Restores 20 HP to user on use

 -Restores all HP to user

 -When used; Resistance + 5 for the rest of the chapter

 -When used; Max HP + 5 for the rest of the chapter

 -When used; Strength + 2 for the rest of the chapter

 -Raises Movement by 2 Permanently

Divine Dragon Tears (1/1) 5000 G
 -Raises Max HP by 5, All Other Stats by 2 Permanently

Arms Scroll (1/1) 2500 G 
 -Raises all displayed weapon skills by one level

Second Seal (1/1) 2500 G
 -This allows you to swap to alternate classes after a unit is above Level 10.
 All stats are maintained (with a few differences that will be shown when
 doing so). You can switch back to your old class later on too. This is
 useful for gathering skills on one unit as well as increasing their overall
 stats and weapon levels. Check the class section, as well as the character
 section, and the skill section for more! If a Class 2 unit, you can go back
 to Class 1 of that Unit tree too. A very useful item.

Master Seal (1/1) 2500 G
 -This allows you to upgrade to a Class 2 unit from a Class 1 unit, as long as
 you are above Level 10. (Ex: Mercenary --> Hero). It is only one way. It is
 used nicely with Change Seals, going up to the top of the tree then changing
 either back to the bottom, or the bottom/middle of another unit tree!

Gold (S) ---- 2000
 -Sells for 1,000G

Gold (M) 10,000
 -Sells for 5,000G

Gold (L) 20,000
 -Sells for 10,000G

Sweet Medicine (3/3) ----G 
 -Restores HP by 5

 -When used; Strength, Skill and Speed +2 until end of Chapter

Chris's Home-made Sweets (5/5) ----G
 -When used; Max HP +5, Defense and Resistance +2 until end of Chapter

Tiki's Tears (1/1) ----G
 -When used; Max HP +5, all other stats +2 until end of Chapter

Seed of Trust (1/1) ----G
 -When used, boosts support gain when doubled with another unit

Scented Box (1/1) 4800 G
 -Makes corpse armies (skirmishes) appear on the World Map when used

Space-Time Gate (1/1) ----G
 -Makes travelling merchants appear on the World Map when used

Demon Fighter Scroll (1/1) ----G (DLC)
 -Changes a Level 10 or above unit to the Demon Fighter class

All stats +2 Book (1/1) ---- G
 -Teaches a Skill that Adds + 2 to each stat while equipped

Ultimate Emblem (1/1)
 -Reward for achieving max Fame. Sells for 99,999G

Other-world Item (1/1) ----G (DLC)
 -When the item is DLC only and the other player doesn't have it, it will
  appear as this

==============================================================================
WEAPONS                                                                 [WPNS]
==============================================================================

This section lists the weapons, their stats, and any notes that are needed!

Format:

(Weapon types will be per section)

Weapon Name  | Mt | Hit | Crt | Rng | Use | Value | Effect | Lv |

Weapon Name: The weapon name
Mt: Weapon Power
Hit: Weapon Accuracy
Crt: The weapon's critical rate
Use: How many times the weapon can be used without breaking
Value: The value in a shop
Effect: Any effects will be noted
Lv: The weapon level requirement to use it

Quick Weapon Search!:

==============================================================================
EXTRAS                                                                  [EXTR]
==============================================================================

This section will detail the various Extras in the game.

SpotPass Content:

This is just a reference to all the things avaliable in the Bonus Box (found
within the "Wireless" menu).

You may have to do "Update Now" in order to see below.

This is current as of 4/18/13.

Bonus Teams:

These are spotpass teams from previous games. All team leaders can be
recruited, as well as fought as many times as you want. The teams are built
up in ways sometimes familiar with players of previous games.

An example is Nino's team from FE7, she's with a Hero, Swordmaster, and
Assassin, which could represent Linus, Lloyd, and Jaffar, for instance. Or
Lyn's crew being the characters you get in Lyn's story, or Nergal's team the
Black Fang. Fun little references like that.

I will not include their skills/stats as you can view them yourself, and
it will make the list cleaner this way.

Note that the characters often will have special skills and stats, though.

            "May halve enemy Def/Res when attacking. Trigger % = (Skill Stat)

            "May add half the wielder's accrued damage to attacks. Trigger %
             = (Skill Stat x 2)

==============================================================================
SUPPORT ARCHIVE                                                         [SPPT]
==============================================================================

Unlike previous FIre Emblem games, supports in this work in a slightly
different way.

There is no maximum limit of 5 supports per play through, the only limitation
is one "S" support (marriage), but the rest can be filled up.

Rather than the amount of turns that pass with units next to each other, or
the amount of times units appear on the same map together, in this the
supports come about as a result of the relationship status (the hearts that
appear above the heads of units next to each other).

Seed of Trust, Event Tiles, and conversations in the barracks also help
relationships improve. Supports boost supporting units' stats when fighting
together or near each other.

They also lead to special epilogues if married. Whether these epilogues will
be listed below is up to the readers. Maybe they should in character profiles
instead?

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
LIST OF SUPPORTS

Note: MyUnit supports *everyone*, and can marry *anyone* of the opposite
      gender, including Generation II units.
Note: MyUnit's support conversations are sometimes the same for both male
      and female, or very similar. S ranks differ, however.
Note: Children supports' with their fathers are often the same. The only
      things that vary are the father's lines/responses, but the children
      will have the same lines most of the time. Sometimes even the responses
      are *exactly* the same. (For instance, Inigo being Chrom's son will
      have almost the *exact* conversation as if Inigo were, say, Libra's
      son). The compilation may support this.
Note: Sibling supports' are often similar situations, with some variations
      in dialogue. (For instance; Lucina and Inigo as siblings have the
      same situation as Lucina and Morgan (Male) as siblings; just with some
      very small differences).

Tips for 100% Completing the Support Archive:
-Preferrably second playthrough to already have the archive and keep track
 of what supports you do and do not have.
-Play either Casual mode, or make sure another save file is open if playing
 Classic.
-Make a save file that has all A supports but no S's. Preferrably one before
 Chapter 13 (where Chrom is forced to marry).
-Now, get S supports with different parirings, but do NOT save on the same
 file, instead, save on a spare file. (IF casual mode, then on-map "Save" will
 work.)
-Reload the original file, get S supports with different pairings, and repeat
 the above process.
-In the Support Archive, all those S supports should be recorded!
-If you have Seeds of Trust, then you can keep using them, get the supports,
 save on a separate file, then redo this method for different pairs. This is
 much quicker then building it up manually, try to have at least 4 in stock.

Note: The issue with the above method is that the second generation has
      special supports depending on the parents --these are the ones that will
      be harded to get as a result, but you can continue from that save file
      and mix up pairings to ensure you don't have to keep playing through
      from the first chapter to get all the different parirings.

You can find the transcripts for the supports here, courtesy of user Misha-
Heart!

http://www.gamefaqs.com/3ds/643003-fire-emblem-awakening/faqs/66787

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ENDINGS

This is where endings, individual/married will be posted. This section will
likely take long times to update too due to the variety and possiblities,
though I will seek help to ensure it is completed faster, if ever.

Note: Like with supports, many endings follow a pattern and are often the
      same. The father usually has a set epilogue, and the wife's story will
      vary.
Note: MyUnit has the same epilogue depending on gender, regardless of who the
      wife or husband is (with a few exceptions).

==============================================================================
GENERAL STRATEGIES/OTHER/WORLD MAP/ETC!                                 [OTHR]

This section will contain strategies and tips for use in general! There will
be small other things like terrain bonuses and things like that too!

Event Tiles ------------------------------------------------------------------

As serenesforest calls them, these are the sparkling gold tiles on the map.

You can get various rewards by waiting on them. If doubled and capable of
supporting, a unit's relationship may improve.

Otherwise, you may get EXP, or weapon EXP.

Lastly, you can acquire many items, the same as random items acquired from
the Barracks. Below is the list (from serenesforest.net) by category:

World Map --------------------------------------------------------------------

There will also be the completed world map and all the translations, but for
now Serenes Forest has a very convenient (and beautiful!) map with already
translated locations, so until I get around to writing my own, please redirect
your attention to this wonderful site!:

http://www.serenesforest.net/fe13/world.html

World Map Location Data -------------------------------------------------------

This section will give information on a location in the game. The map and
the stores are provided. (The map will have no enemies on it as skirmishes
may vary).

Some notes are made regarding how to unlock a map if needed, such as a
sidequest requirement.

You can begin buying items from the world map after Chapter 4. You can revisit
older areas, such as DLC maps and story chapters you have finished, and there
will be a list of items on display that you can buy. You can also forge
weapons, or sell items/weapons at these locations as well. This list does
not include wandering merchants (yet).

For weapon/item descriptions, check their respective sections. I provide
the same stats from the above lists, and Japanese characters so you know
which item is being referred to. Alternately, you can probably tell by the
price, or the weapon/item logo anyway.

Template:

Note: "Value" corresponds to the price in the store. If the selected character
has a Silver Card (avaliable in DLC), item/weapon price is halved.
Note: To find the corresponding location, when on an area on the map, look
at the top right to see what Chapter this location was used in, and find
it on the list below.

Note: When a wandering merchant appears, some items are added with a sparkle,
once an item is purchased the merchant disapepars and will reappear later.

Location Name (Localized)
Chapter this map is on

Notes: IF any.

Store from world map:
(For Weapons)

Weapon Name  | Mt | Hit | Crt | Rng | Use | Value | Effect    | Lv |

(For Items)
Item Name (Uses/Max Uses) Cost G Japanese Characters
 -Description

Map of location.

==============================================================================
CLOSING/CREDITS/CONTACT INFORMATION                                      [CCC]
==============================================================================

Fire Emblem games can be pretty in depth, so as you can imagine, this FAQ will
be constantly updating with more Chapters and information as time goes on!

I'm aware the character section is missing skills that the characters start
with, I will be sure to include this for Generation I characters at least
(as inheritance can get complicated) in future updates!

If you have any suggestions, or anything that may be helpful to other readers,
or see an error even as small as a typo, please feel free to email me! I like
the FAQ to be as easy to read and error free as possible, but obviously cannot
find all these on my own!

Likewise, if you have strategies you would like to add that work nicely for
some maps (as I do not have a lot of strategies listed yet), feel free to
email them and I will credit you for the contribution!

If you thought the FAQ was helpful, please recommend it to others who may
want to use it too!

Thanks for reading, cheers!

-MKay

CREDITS:

Thanks to user ryusashi for helping with small tidbits here and there with
the FAQ!

Thanks to users who emailed me suggestions for better search terms and
general feedback!

Thanks to users on the Kakusei board for contributing some ideas for the FAQ,
as well as responding/answering in a timely manner! I will be sure to provide
a link to their own likely wonderful FAQs whenever they end up posting them,
for those who do!

Thanks to serenesforest for a lot of information I used that they had already
translated and put in more localized terms! If you see anything that cross
lists with their site, it's no coincedence!

Thanks to the Official Fire Emblem: Kakusei Guidebook for providing many
things such as stat minimum/maximum for classes and the like!

Thanks to gameFAQs for hosting this!

Thanks to you, the reader, because it'd be a lot of effort for nothing if
there was no one who was getting help from this, neh? I really enjoyed writing
it regardless!

CONTACT:

Email me at: mkaykitkats@live.com

I read all emails, and respond if necessary. I really do!

==============================================================================
VERSION INFO                                                             [VIN]
==============================================================================

Version 0.00 [04/19/2012]: Version 0.00 (When the game was released)

Version 0.50 [05/20/2012]: Version 0.50 First FAQ posting. Contains a lot of
                           vital translations, such as basic actions, menu
                           translations, etc. The general set up to how the
                           walkthrough will be is explained. Character guide
                           has mostly complete Generation I characters, with
                           others in progress. A basic class list and all
                           skills are provided, with some Japanese characters
                           pending to be added.

Version 0.55 [5/24/2012]: Version 0.55 contains a complete Character Guide for
                          Generations I and II, as well as DLC characters up
                          to May 17th. The Class section has been completed
                          minus opinions on each. Opinions on all characters
                          are still in progress. All normal class skills have
                          their respective Japanese characters added. Basic
                          items and their value have also been added, all
                          Fame bonus rewards posted. All swords have been
                          posted in the weapons section.

Version 0.60 [6/10/2012]: Completed the Weapons Section with the Japanese
                          characters as well. Added some Terrain translations
                          and effects in the Vital Translations section. Got
                          to the end of Chapter 3 in the Walkthrough. The
                          walkthrough will be the focus from now on with the
                          other sections secondary until completed (however
                          if other sections need work in some aspects or if
                          you have suggestions, please contact me!) Sidequest
                          Chapter 1 has been added as well.

Version 0.65 [6/15/2012]: Completed up to the end of Chapter 5 of the main
                          story, and the second sidequest. Began the World
                          Map data section; containing shops and simplified
                          map for Chapters completed in the walkthrough,
                          including sidequests. Minor corrections to weapons
                          and items were made.

Version 0.68 [7/12/2012]: Decided to take a different approach: Chapter maps
                          and recruitable units are given priority, and the
                          tips/walkthrough details themselves will be posted
                          after all maps are posted. This will ensure a
                          quicker, and smoother update. Chapters up to the
                          end of 13 have full maps with details. The shops
                          have been updated. Sidequests 6-16 will likely
                          be focused on for the next update before the main
                          story walkthrough continues. One DLC chapter per
                          update may be put in place as not to fall too far
                          behind.

Version 0.70 [8/22/2012]: Maps up to Sidequest 17, and Chapter 14 of the main
                          story are completed. The walkthrough will wait until
                          all maps are completed. Minor edits, corrections in
                          character guide. Some of the map specific guides
                          have the map but lack the shop details that will
                          appear next update. 

Version 1.00 [11/07/2012]: Phew! That took too long, outside work has been
                           really busy. As you can see, all levels have
                           their basic information/some strategies done, as
                           well as Sidequests up to 17 which covers all those
                           you get to the end of the story. All that is left
                           for future updates is the remaining sidequests,
                           and possibly the large amounts of DLC. The official
                           English names, when they come out, will be updated
                           accordingly.

Version 1.05 [01/17/2013]: Began adding English names in addition to the
                           Japanese ones in anticipation of the US release on
                           February 4th, 2013.

Version 1.05 [02/06/2013]: With the official US copy, I am going through the
                           lengthy adjusting process, and will now aim to
                           finish this guide 100%! Any and all help to doing
                           so is appreciated, and you will be credited
                           accordingly.

Version 1.10 [02/10/2013]: Started detailing maps in the sidequests, as well
                           as guides up to Chapter 13's end. I added a support
                           archive section that I will put in as soon as the
                           main walkthrough is done. But if anyone wants to
                           help compile, please see contact section. Began
                           adding Character Names, opinions, localized skill
                           names, etc as well!

Version 1.50 [02/13/2013]: The FAQ had a complete overhaul -- no longer in
                           shift_jis format, for reader convenience and ease
                           of reading. The Japanese characters have since been
                           removed, or in the process of being removed (such
                           as in the sub sections).

Version 1.75 [02/18/2013]: The Walkthrough is fully completed. The sidequests
                           that are avaliable up to now are completed. All
                           previous Japanese characters have been localized to
                           the US version of the game. All that is left is
                           the complete character opinions and the collection
                           of Support Conversations.

Version 1.80 [02/28/2013]: All sidequests up to current date, still some
                           final walkthrough things and DLC chapters to iron
                           out, and lastly class commentaries, but otherwise
                           done~ Just two more sidequests to go!
